Treasure Companion\r\n\r\nProduction-oriented foundation and fully automated local demo for a private nautical-fantasy date-night Tall Tale. All committed story material is generic development seed content; no final surprise content belongs in this public repository.\r\n\r\n## Current phase\r\n\r\nThe application is now a unified Tall Tale platform. The cinematic gateway opens distinct Player, Captain, and Creator workspaces without treating role choice as authorization. Players have durable identities, invitation acceptance, a multi-voyage library, live waiting/runtime state, and exact-version archives. Captains can create version-pinned crew voyages, deliver individually hashed link/QR/code/PIN invitations, manage invitation lifecycle, preview the Player-safe surface, and launch accepted crews. Creator Studio retains immutable publishing and now adds structured version comparison, restore-to-draft, and fork provenance.\r\n\r\nThe original companion and expanded Game Master Command Center remain integrated compatibility surfaces. A shared animation director coordinates the harbor, journal, chart, artifact, gateway, and finale experiences without allowing presentation timing to outrun server truth. All committed content remains fictional development seed material.\r\n\r\n## Stack\r\n\r\n- Next.js 16 App Router, React 19, strict TypeScript\r\n- Prisma 6.19.3 with SQLite for local/test and an equivalent MySQL production schema\r\n- GSAP 3.15 for orchestrated scenes and SVG/text work; Motion 12 for React interaction and presence\r\n- StPageFlip for the journal; local Rive and Lottie runtimes with explicit static fallbacks\r\n- bcrypt password/access-code hashing, server-side database sessions, CSRF tokens, and rate limiting\r\n- Vitest and Playwright\r\n\r\n## Reproducible setup\r\n\r\nRequirements: Windows PowerShell 5.1+, Node.js 24, npm 11, and Git. Existing campaign progress is preserved across normal stop/start cycles. Network/UNC workspaces are mirrored to an ignored local runtime under `%LOCALAPPDATA%` because Node and SQLite are unreliable on network shares. Stop it with `npm run dev:stop`.\r\n\r\n- Role gateway: `http://127.0.0.1:3000/`\r\n- Player: `http://127.0.0.1:3000/tale/development-forever-treasure`\r\n- Player library: `http://127.0.0.1:3000/player`\r\n- Tall Tale catalog: `http://127.0.0.1:3000/tales`\r\n- Player phrase: `development-moonwake`\r\n- Returning Player development login: `sera` / the configured `PLAYER_PASSWORD` (or `PLAYER_ACCESS_CODE` fallback)\r\n- GM: `http://127.0.0.1:3000/quartermaster`\r\n- Studio: `http://127.0.0.1:3000/studio`\r\n- Captain: `http://127.0.0.1:3000/captain`\r\n- GM development[REDACTED: LOGIN CREDENTIAL]\r\n\r\nThese values are disposable local defaults, never production credentials. Creates `.env` only when absent; existing local configuration is preserved and validated.\r\n3. Refuses to take an occupied port, starts the server as a hidden recorded process, and waits for an HTTP health response.\r\n7. Prints the player and GM URLs, disposable credentials, and stop command.\r\n\r\nRun `npm run dev:stop` before switching branches or replacing the runtime. It does not create a second product or a browser-owned capture implementation.\r\n\r\n```text\r\nShared /vision-companion React surface\r\n  -> DesktopCapturePlatformAdapter -> restricted context-isolated IPC ---+\r\n  -> WebCapturePlatformAdapter -> paired loopback WebSocket -------------+\r\n                                                                       CompanionCoordinator\r\n                                                                         -> one CaptureCore\r\n                                                                            -> ElectronTargetProvider\r\n                                                                            -> sandboxed CaptureWorker\r\n                                                                            -> bounded quality/ring pipeline\r\n                                                                            -> CompanionStorage\r\n                                                                            -> Windows health/hotkey monitor\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe React layer gathers user intent and renders state. Chromium may select a supported Windows backend internally; B-2 does not claim a particular backend as an application guarantee.\r\n\r\n## Capture state machine\r\n\r\nThe allowed states are `IDLE`, `PAIRING`, `READY`, `TARGET_SELECTION_REQUIRED`, `TARGET_SELECTED`, `STARTING`, `CAPTURING`, `PAUSED`, `FINALIZING`, `PROCESSING_CAPTURE`, `COMPLETED`, `CANCELLED`, `FAILED`, and `TARGET_LOST`.\r\n\r\nEvery transition is validated, sequenced, timestamped, correlated to a session where applicable, emitted as an event, and written to structured logs. Duplicate stop returns the prior metadata-only completion for the same session. Stale session IDs are rejected. A minimized or closed target becomes `TARGET_LOST`; restore can return a retained valid target to `TARGET_SELECTED`. A closed HWND invalidates the target.\r\n\r\n## Target semantics\r\n\r\n- Only `desktopCapturer.getSources({types: [\"window\"]})` candidates are accepted.\r\n- The user explicitly confirms a current enumerated source; a likely Sea of Thieves label is convenience only.\r\n- Full display capture is not offered.\r\n- Candidate titles are sanitized and bounded. Ordinary logs never receive the title.\r\n- Small selection thumbnails are capped; native frames are not serialized as JSON.\r\n- B-2 targets are process-session-only. `remember: true` is rejected, and the target expires on Companion exit or invalid HWND.\r\n- The HWND helper reports client size, minimized/restored state, and closure every 500 ms while a target exists, even when the global hotkey is disabled.\r\n\r\n## Frame and queue architecture\r\n\r\nThe worker samples a native-size selected-window stream into `320x180` RGBA analysis frames. Electron IPC transfers binary typed arrays. Player mode inserts them into a deterministic oldest-first ring with both a frame ceiling and a 32 MiB byte ceiling. The default is 5 seconds at 10 samples/second; the governed range is 3-8 seconds and 8-12 samples/second. The ring can retain at most 84 frames.\r\n\r\nQuality processing derives luminance, clipping, contrast, entropy, sharpness proxy, perceptual hash, near-duplicate distance, and adjacent-frame motion. Selection uses temporal buckets and perceptual diversity, preserves chronology, and returns at most 12 frame references. Continuous duplicates produce a frozen-stream result.\r\n\r\nThe B-2 capture-only consumer completes before `BoundedFrameRing.clear()` zero-fills pixel and luminance buffers. No raw player frame is written to disk, sent to the Next server, returned in protocol JSON, or retained after completion/cancel/error/shutdown.\r\n\r\nCreator mode uses the same stream and quality path. MediaRecorder WebM chunks are drained in order into an app-managed `.part` file, capped at 2 GiB. Stop waits for asynchronous final MediaRecorder data before hashing/finalization. The completed artifact and sidecar use generated IDs; cancellation and failure remove the temporary file.\r\n\r\n## Initial performance budgets\r\n\r\n| Resource                   | Budget                                             |\r\n| -------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------- |\r\n| Player raw-frame memory    | 32 MiB hard byte ceiling                           |\r\n| Player ring                | 84 frames maximum                                  |\r\n| Player duration            | 3-8 seconds; 5-second default                      |\r\n| Analysis rate              | 8-12 FPS; 10 FPS default                           |\r\n| Evidence selection         | 3-12 metadata frame references; normal target 6-12 |\r\n| Creator media              | 2 GiB hard ceiling; 10-minute command ceiling      |\r\n| Pairing request body       | 32 KiB                                             |\r\n| Incoming WebSocket message | 64 KiB                                             |\r\n| Target candidates          | 64 maximum; bounded thumbnails/icons               |\r\n| Authentication             | 10-second socket proof timeout                     |\r\n| Command response           | 20-second browser adapter timeout                  |\r\n\r\nThe deterministic Electron harness measured five repeated scans with no orphan `.part` files, no active recording/worker session, and a 10,425,975-byte external-memory delta in the final recorded run. This is a harness measurement, not a Sea of Thieves gameplay-stutter claim.\r\n\r\n## Capability and degradation model\r\n\r\nCapabilities report OS/CPU/memory, Electron GPU devices, encoder candidates, hardware-acceleration observation, CPU metadata fallback, protocol/package versions, storage category/free bytes, modes, resolutions, preview behavior, hotkey support, and privacy budgets. They explicitly report `localInference: false`, `locationVerification: false`, and `cloudBuild: false`.\r\n\r\nExclusive-fullscreen reliability is not claimed. If the selected source stops, closes, minimizes, or freezes, B-2 returns a capture error or insufficient-capture result and recommends restore or Borderless Windowed. It never uses injection as a fallback.\r\n\r\n## B-1 compatibility seam\r\n\r\nThe historical deterministic B-1 verifier remains available only as a development/test consumer. Its result endpoint is gated by `mock_verification_consumer`, which defaults off in production, and packaged Electron rejects legacy mock preparation. B-2 capture results never become B-1 verification results implicitly.\r\nFILE=Development_Docs\\AR\\Phase_B2\\B2_Protocol.md\r\n# Phase B-2 Capture Protocol 2.0\r\n\r\n## Envelope\r\n\r\nBoth adapters use the same logical contract. Desktop IPC supplies a command plus validated payload directly; browser transport uses this strict envelope:\r\n\r\n```json\r\n{\r\n  \"protocolVersion\": \"2.0\",\r\n  \"messageType\": \"capture.command\",\r\n  \"messageId\": \"message_...\",\r\n  \"requestId\": \"request_...\",\r\n  \"sessionId\": \"pairing_...\",\r\n  \"timestamp\": \"2026-07-18T07:30:00.000Z\",\r\n  \"sequence\": 1,\r\n  \"payload\": {\r\n    \"command\": \"capture.scan.start\",\r\n    \"input\": {\r\n      \"requestId\": \"request_player_scan\",\r\n      \"attemptId\": \"attempt_player_scan\",\r\n      \"durationMs\": 5000,\r\n      \"sampleFps\": 10,\r\n      \"minimumFrames\": 6\r\n    }\r\n  }\r\n}\r\n```\r\n\r\nUnknown envelope and command fields are rejected. Browser sequences must increase, request IDs cannot repeat, and the pairing origin/protocol must match.\r\n\r\n## Operations\r\n\r\n| Group                          | Commands                                                                                         |\r\n| ------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |\r\n| Capability/status              | `capture.getCapabilities`, `capture.getStatus`                                                   |\r\n| Target                         | `capture.listTargets`, `capture.selectTarget`                                                    |\r\n| Creator                        | `capture.creator.start`, `.pause`, `.resume`, `.stop`, `.cancel`, `.list`, `.preview`, `.delete` |\r\n| Player                         | `capture.scan.start`, `.stop`, `.cancel`                                                         |\r\n| Privacy                        | `capture.privacy.pause`, `.resume`                                                               |\r\n| Desktop hotkey                 | `capture.hotkey.configure`, `.disable`                                                           |\r\n| Desktop pairing administration | `capture.pairing.pending`, `.approve`, `.list`, `.revoke`                                        |\r\n| Diagnostics                    | `capture.diagnostic.create`, `.export`                                                           |\r\n\r\nThe browser allowlist omits hotkey configuration and pairing administration. Preview and diagnostic export return short-lived, exact-origin token URLs to one managed artifact; they never accept a path.\r\n\r\n## Events\r\n\r\nAuthenticated browser clients and the desktop renderer receive `status`, `state`, `capture-progress`, `capture-completed`, and `capture-error`. A fresh WebSocket first receives `companion.challenge` and cannot send capture commands before successful authentication.\r\n\r\n## Pairing proof\r\n\r\n1. Browser generates an ECDSA P-256 key pair and sends only the public JWK with an allowed exact origin.\r\n2. Desktop shows that origin and a random six-digit, two-minute code.\r\n3. User approves in desktop and enters the code in the browser.\r\n4. The pairing is origin-bound, expires after 30 minutes, and persists only public/replay metadata.\r\n5. WebSocket sends a 256-bit random challenge.\r\n6. Browser signs `challenge|pairingId|origin|2.0` with ECDSA P-256/SHA-256.\r\n7. Revocation closes matching sockets; expiration, signature failure, reused challenge, duplicate request ID, or non-increasing sequence is rejected.\r\n\r\nNo pairing secret, code, signature, cookie, or private key is logged or stored by the Companion.\r\n\r\n## Capture-only result\r\n\r\nThe only B-2 result values are:\r\n\r\n- `EVIDENCE_CAPTURED`\r\n- `INSUFFICIENT_CAPTURE_EVIDENCE`\r\n- `CAPTURE_CANCELLED`\r\n- `CAPTURE_ERROR`\r\n\r\nRepresentative player completion:\r\n\r\n```json\r\n{\r\n  \"sessionId\": \"scan_...\",\r\n  \"result\": \"EVIDENCE_CAPTURED\",\r\n  \"reasons\": pairing.allowedOrigin !== origin) throw captureError(\"PAIRING_REQUIRED\", \"Pairing is required.\");\r\n    if (pairing.revokedAt) throw captureError(\"PAIRING_REVOKED\", \"Pairing was revoked.\");\r\n    if (Date.parse(pairing.expiresAt) <= Date.now()) throw captureError(\"PAIRING_EXPIRED\", \"Pairing expired.\");\r\n    return pairing;\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  #expirePending() {\r\n    const now = Date.now();\r\n    for (const [id, pending] of this.pending) if (Date.parse(pending.expiresAt) <= now) this.pending.delete(id);\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  async #persist() {\r\n    const operation = this.persistPromise\r\n      .catch(() => {})\r\n      .then(async () => {\r\n        const temporary = `${this.filePath}.${crypto.randomUUID()}.tmp`;\r\n        const serializable = [...this.pairings.values()].map((pairing) => ({\r\n          ...pairing,\r\n          requestIds: [...pairing.requestIds].slice(-500),\r\n        }));\r\n        try {\r\n          await this.filePath);\r\n        } finally {\r\n          await fsp.rm(temporary, { force: true }).catch(() => {});\r\n        }\r\n      });\r\n    this.persistPromise = operation;\r\n    return operation;\r\n  }\r\n}\r\n\r\nclass SlidingRateLimiter {\r\n  constructor(limit = 30, windowMs = 10_000) {\r\n    this.limit = limit;\r\n    this.windowMs = windowMs;\r\n    this.entries = new tests.\\r\\n\\r\\n## 15.4 Stale-stage protection\\r\\n\\r\\nBefore delivering a result:\\r\\n\\r\\n* confirm the story session still exists;\\r\\n* confirm the stage is still active;\\r\\n* confirm the waypoint version still matches;\\r\\n* confirm the attempt has not been cancelled or replaced.\\r\\n\\r\\nA delayed result from a previous stage must be rejected as stale.\\r\\n\\r\\n---\\r\\n\\r\\n# 16. No injection fallback exists.\\n+- Windows 11 x64 is the implemented platform. Other Windows builds/hardware and non-Windows systems are not certified by this run.\\n+- Creator recording uses Chromium MediaRecorder WebM/VP9 where available. Capabilities report candidates and CPU metadata fallback; B-2 does not promise a dedicated hardware encoder.\\n+- The final unsigned package is blocked by this host's Application Control policy. This is the best default for desktop apps with weak accessibility trees.\\\\r\\\\n- If you need accessibility text or element indexes, call `get_window_state({ window, include_screenshot: false, include_text: true })`. Use `sky.scroll({ window, x, y, scrollX: 0, scrollY: 600 })` to scroll down from `(x, y)`. Negative `scrollY` scrolls up; negative `scrollX` scrolls left. Do not pass `element_index` to `scroll`; if a specific pane needs focus, click it first with coordinates, then scroll from inside that pane.\\\\r\\\\n- Use keyboard navigation when it is faster than hunting UI pixels.\\\\r\\\\n- For text entry into a document, slide, sheet, editor, or canvas, foreground process metadata and window title are not enough. Use the actual repository path on the current machine; no source file contains the example path above.\n\n## Window does not appear\n\n- Make sure the application owns a normal visible Windows window and is not minimized.\n- Press **Select Game Window** again; B-2 never selects by process/title silently.\n- Prefer Sea of Thieves Borderless Windowed if exclusive fullscreen is absent or frozen.\n- If the game restarted, the old HWND is invalid; select the replacement explicitly.\n- A target is intentionally not remembered across Companion restarts.\n\n## Minimized, closed, frozen, or black\n\n- `CAPTURE_SOURCE_MINIMIZED`: restore the selected window. The retained valid HWND should return to selected state.\n- `CAPTURE_SOURCE_CLOSED`: reopen and reselect; closure invalidates the target.\n- `CAPTURE_FRAME_TIMEOUT` or frozen/duplicate warning: restore, expose changing content, use Borderless Windowed, and retry.\n- Mostly black/dark/bright/blurred: change the scene or sweep more slowly. These are capture-quality messages, not a claim that the location is wrong.\n\n## Hotkey fails\n\n- `HOTKEY_CONFLICT` means another application already registered that combination. Choose another preset or use the in-app pointer/Space/Enter control.\n- Application-control policy may block the fixed PowerShell helper; use the in-app control and collect a metadata diagnostic.\n- Disable removes the registration but selected-window health monitoring remains active.\n- Do not use an input-injection tool to test release; press and release the configured physical key.\n\n## Browser cannot pair\n\n- The desktop Companion must be running locally and listening on `127.0.0.1:32179`.\n- Request pairing, approve the exact displayed origin in desktop, then enter the displayed six-digit code before two minutes.\n- Refresh loses the in-memory browser private key by design; request a new pairing.\n- Expired/revoked pairing requires a new ceremony.\n- For nonstandard development/hosted origins, add the exact origin to `TALL_TALE_COMPANION_ALLOWED_ORIGINS`; never use `*`.\n- Keep `NEXT_PUBLIC_COMPANION_URL` on approved `127.0.0.1` or `localhost`; CSP rejects non-loopback values.\n- Browser private-network or mixed-content policies may differ for an HTTPS deployment. Validate the intended production origin/browser before release; do not weaken CORS or bind to LAN as a workaround.\n\n## Creator recording fails\n\n- Check free disk in capabilities and app-data permissions.\n- The hard local file ceiling is 2 GiB and the command duration ceiling is 10 minutes.\n- Stop waits for final encoder chunks. If the encoder/source fails, the `.part` file is removed or cleaned at next startup.\n- Creator manifest server persistence additionally requires a signed-in creator, CSRF, ownership, and a draft waypoint version ID. The local recording remains available if database persistence fails.\n\n## Diagnostics\n\nCreate **metadata-only diagnostic bundle**, then prepare and download its one-time five-minute link. It includes versions, capability/health, transition/error/cleanup, and pairing status without credentials. Raw-frame diagnostics are unavailable in B-2 even with consent.\n\nDo not send the whole Companion user-data directory. Review a diagnostic before sharing it and use the application-managed bundle.\n\n## Safe cleanup\n\nUse creator **Delete** for recordings. Stop the Companion before manual maintenance. Remove only generated validation `dist`, `.desktop-bundle`, or the resolved Electron `userData/companion` child after preserving desired recordings. This choice is recorded in ADR 0002. No route, React component, story engine, or domain model is forked for desktop.\n\nInstall dependencies and run:\n\n```powershell\nnpm ci\nnpm run db:generate\nnpm run db:migrate\nnpx tsx prisma/seed.ts --ensure\nnpm run desktop:dev\n```\n\nThe development command runs Next at `http://127.0.0.1:3000`, waits for it, and opens Electron. The Navigate menu opens the same `/player`, `/captain`, and `/studio` routes used by browsers.\n\n## Restricted native bridge\n\n`contextIsolation`, renderer sandboxing, `nodeIntegration: false`, `webSecurity`, external-window denial, and same-origin navigation are enabled. `preload.cjs` exposes only one frozen method. `commands.cjs` allows exactly:\n\n- `vision.getCapabilities`\n- `vision.prepareMockScan`\n- `app.getDiagnostics`\n\nThe bridge has no generic shell, process, filesystem, registry, network-proxy, or arbitrary IPC command. Identifiers and mock scenarios are allowlisted. The Desktop adapter uses this bridge only for governed desktop capability/preparation, then uses the same authenticated server attempt APIs as web/PWA.\n\nRun boundary tests with `npm run desktop:test`.\n\n## Production package\n\n```powershell\nnpm run desktop:build\n```\n\nThe command runs `next build` with `output: standalone`, stages the standalone server, its traced runtime dependencies, static assets, and public assets under `.desktop-bundle`, and invokes Electron Builder for an NSIS installer. The packaged main process starts that bundled server in an Electron utility process on loopback port 32178 and loads it after a bounded health wait. `npm run desktop:smoke` launches the unpacked package with hidden smoke instrumentation and proves the shared app title/origin/shell version. `.desktop-bundle` and installer output are generated artifacts and must not be committed.\n\nB-1 disables executable signing/editing in the local Electron Builder pipeline so Windows packaging does not depend on privileged symbolic-link creation in the signing-tool cache. The generated installer is therefore intentionally unsigned and uses Electron's default application icon; both must be replaced before a public distribution. B-1 does not access a camera, register global hotkeys, add a tray agent, or install a localhost Companion. Those capabilities remain false and belong to later phases.\n\r\n", "type": "input_text"}]
